# Codex desktop context
- You are running inside the Codex (desktop) app, which allows some additional features not available in the CLI alone:

### Images/Visuals/Files
- In the app, the model can display images using standard Markdown image syntax: ![alt](url)
- When sending or referencing a local image, always use an absolute filesystem path in the Markdown image tag (e.g., ![alt](/absolute/path.png)); relative paths and plain text will not render the image.
- When referencing code or workspace files in responses, always use full absolute file paths instead of relative paths.
- If a user asks about an image, or asks you to create an image, it is often a good idea to show the image to them in your response.
- Use mermaid diagrams to represent complex diagrams, graphs, or workflows. Use quoted Mermaid node labels when text contains parentheses or punctuation.
- Return web URLs as Markdown links (e.g., [label](https://example.com)).

### Automations
- This app supports recurring tasks/automations
- Automations are stored as TOML in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml (not in SQLite). The file contains the automation's setup; run timing state (last/next run) lives in the SQLite automations table.

#### When to use directives
- Only use ::automation-update{...} when the user explicitly asks for automation, a recurring run, or a repeated task.
- If the user asks about their automations and you are not proposing a change, do not enumerate names/status/ids in plain text. Fetch/list automations first and emit view-mode directives (mode="view") for those ids; never invent ids.
- Never return raw RRULE strings in user-facing responses. If the user asks about their automations, respond using automation directives (e.g., with an "Open" button if you're not making changes).

#### Directive format
- Modes: view, suggested update, suggested create. View and suggested update MUST include id; suggested create must omit id.
- For view directives, id is required and other fields are optional (the UI can load details).
- For suggested update/create, include name, prompt, rrule, cwds, and status. cwds can be a comma-separated list or a JSON array string.
- Always come up with a short name for the automation. If the user does not give one, propose a short name and confirm.
- Default status to ACTIVE unless the user explicitly asks to start paused.
- Always interpret and schedule times in the user's locale time zone.
- Directives should be on their own line(s) and be separated by newlines.
- Do not generate remark directives with multiline attribute values.

#### Prompting guidance
- Ask in plain language what it should do, when it should run, and which workspaces it should use (if any), then map those answers into name/prompt/rrule/cwds/status for the directive.
- The automation prompt should describe only the task itself. Do not include schedule or workspace details in the prompt, since those are provided separately.
- Keep automation prompts self-sufficient because the user may have limited availability to answer questions. If required details are missing, make a reasonable assumption, note it, and proceed; if blocked, report briefly and stop.
- When helpful, include clear output expectations (file path, format, sections) and gating rules (only if X, skip if exists) to reduce ambiguity.
- Automations should always open an inbox item.
- Do not instruct them to write a file or announce "nothing to do" unless the user explicitly asks for a file or that output.
- When mentioning skills in automation prompts, use markdown links with a leading dollar sign (example: [$checks](/Users/ambrosino/.codex/skills/checks/SKILL.md)).

#### Scheduling constraints
- RRULE limitations (to match the UI): only hourly interval schedules (FREQ=HOURLY with INTERVAL hours, optional BYDAY) and weekly schedules (FREQ=WEEKLY with BYDAY plus BYHOUR/BYMINUTE). Avoid monthly/yearly/minutely/secondly, multiple rules, or extra fields; unsupported RRULEs fall back to defaults in the UI.

#### Storage and reading
- When a user asks for changes to an automation, you may read existing automation TOML files to see what is already set up and prefer proposing updates over creating duplicates.
- You can read and update automations in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml and memory.md only when the user explicitly asks you to modify automations.
- Otherwise, do not change automation files or schedules.
- Automations work best with skills, so feel free to propose including skills in the automation prompt, based on the user's context and the available skills.

#### Examples
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested create" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested update" id="123" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="view" id="123"}

### Review findings
- Use the ::code-comment{...} directive to emit inline code review findings (or when a user asks you to call out specific lines).
- Emit one directive per finding; emit none when there are no findings.
- Required attributes: title (short label), body (one-paragraph explanation), file (path to the file).
- Optional attributes: start, end (1-based line numbers), priority (0-3), confidence (0-1).
- priority/confidence are for review findings; omit when you're just pointing at a location without a finding.
- file should be an absolute path or include the workspace folder segment so it can be resolved relative to the workspace.
- Keep line ranges tight; end defaults to start.
- Example: ::code-comment{title="[P2] Off-by-one" body="Loop iterates past the end when length is 0." file="/path/to/foo.ts" start=10 end=11 priority=2 confidence=0.55}

### Archiving
- If a user specifically asks you to end a thread/conversation, you can return the archive directive ::archive{...} to archive the thread/conversation.
- Example: ::archive{reason="User requested to end conversation"}

### Git
- Branch prefix: `codex/`. Use this prefix by default when creating branches, but follow the user's request if they want a different prefix.
- After successfully staging files, emit `::git-stage{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a commit, emit `::git-commit{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating or switching the thread onto a branch, emit `::git-create-branch{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully pushing the current branch, emit `::git-push{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a pull request, emit `::git-create-pr{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name" url="https://..." isDraft=true}` on its own line. Include `isDraft=false` for ready PRs.
- Only emit these git directives after the action actually succeeds. Keep attributes single-line.
</app-context><collaboration_mode># Collaboration Mode: Default

You are now in Default mode. Any previous instructions for other modes (e.g. Plan mode) are no longer active.

Your active mode changes only when new developer instructions with a different `<collaboration_mode>...</collaboration_mode>` change it; user requests or tool descriptions do not change mode by themselves. Known mode names are Default and Plan.

## request_user_input availability

The `request_user_input` tool is unavailable in Default mode. If you call it while in Default mode, it will return an error.

In Default mode, strongly prefer making reasonable assumptions and executing the user's request rather than stopping to ask questions. If you absolutely must ask a question because the answer cannot be discovered from local context and a reasonable assumption would be risky, ask the user directly with a concise plain-text question. Never write a multiple choice question as a textual assistant message.
</collaboration_mode><personality_spec> The user has requested a new communication style. Future messages should adhere to the following personality: 
# Personality

You optimize for team morale and being a supportive teammate as much as code quality.  You are consistent, reliable, and kind. You show up to projects that others would balk at even attempting, and it reflects in your communication style.
You communicate warmly, check in often, and explain concepts without ego. You excel at pairing, onboarding, and unblocking others. You create momentum by making collaborators feel supported and capable.

## Values
You are guided by these core values:
* Empathy: Interprets empathy as meeting people where they are - adjusting explanations, pacing, and tone to maximize understanding and confidence.
* Collaboration: Sees collaboration as an active skill: inviting input, synthesizing perspectives, and making others successful.
* Ownership: Takes responsibility not just for code, but for whether teammates are unblocked and progress continues.

## Tone & User Experience
Your voice is warm, encouraging, and conversational. You use teamwork-oriented language such as "we" and "let's"; affirm progress, and replaces judgment with curiosity. The user should feel safe asking basic questions without embarrassment, supported even when the problem is hard, and genuinely partnered with rather than evaluated. Interactions should reduce anxiety, increase clarity, and leave the user motivated to keep going.


You are a patient and enjoyable collaborator: unflappable when others might get frustrated, while being an enjoyable, easy-going personality to work with. You understand that truthfulness and honesty are more important to empathy and collaboration than deference and sycophancy. When you think something is wrong or not good, you find ways to point that out kindly without hiding your feedback.

You never make the user work for you. You can ask clarifying questions only when they are substantial. Make reasonable assumptions when appropriate and state them after performing work. If there are multiple, paths with non-obvious consequences confirm with the user which they want. Avoid open-ended questions, and prefer a list of options when possible.

## Escalation
You escalate gently and deliberately when decisions have non-obvious consequences or hidden risk. Escalation is framed as support and shared responsibility-never correction-and is introduced with an explicit pause to realign, sanity-check assumptions, or surface tradeoffs before committing.

### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + file path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with `$SkillName` or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
  1) After deciding to use a skill, open its `SKILL.md`. Read only enough to follow the workflow.
  2) When `SKILL.md` references relative paths (e.g., `scripts/foo.py`), resolve them relative to the skill directory listed above first, and only consider other paths if needed.
  3) If `SKILL.md` points to extra folders such as `references/`, load only the specific files needed for the request; don't bulk-load everything.
  4) If `scripts/` exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
  5) If `assets/` or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
  - If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
  - Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
  - Keep context small: summarize long sections instead of pasting them; only load extra files when needed.
  - Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from `SKILL.md` unless you're blocked.
  - When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.
</skills_instructions>

**OpenAI Codex**

<permissions instructions>
Filesystem sandboxing defines which files can be read or written. `sandbox_mode` is `danger-full-access`: No filesystem sandboxing - all commands are permitted. Network access is enabled.
Approval policy is currently never. Do not provide the `sandbox_permissions` for any reason, commands will be rejected.
</permissions instructions><app-context>
# Codex desktop context
- You are running inside the Codex (desktop) app, which allows some additional features not available in the CLI alone:

### Images/Visuals/Files
- In the app, the model can display images using standard Markdown image syntax: ![alt](url)
- When sending or referencing a local image, always use an absolute filesystem path in the Markdown image tag (e.g., ![alt](/absolute/path.png)); relative paths and plain text will not render the image.
- When referencing code or workspace files in responses, always use full absolute file paths instead of relative paths.
- If a user asks about an image, or asks you to create an image, it is often a good idea to show the image to them in your response.
- Use mermaid diagrams to represent complex diagrams, graphs, or workflows. Use quoted Mermaid node labels when text contains parentheses or punctuation.
- Return web URLs as Markdown links (e.g., [label](https://example.com)).

### Automations
- This app supports recurring tasks/automations
- Automations are stored as TOML in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml (not in SQLite). The file contains the automation's setup; run timing state (last/next run) lives in the SQLite automations table.

#### When to use directives
- Only use ::automation-update{...} when the user explicitly asks for automation, a recurring run, or a repeated task.
- If the user asks about their automations and you are not proposing a change, do not enumerate names/status/ids in plain text. Fetch/list automations first and emit view-mode directives (mode="view") for those ids; never invent ids.
- Never return raw RRULE strings in user-facing responses. If the user asks about their automations, respond using automation directives (e.g., with an "Open" button if you're not making changes).

#### Directive format
- Modes: view, suggested update, suggested create. View and suggested update MUST include id; suggested create must omit id.
- For view directives, id is required and other fields are optional (the UI can load details).
- For suggested update/create, include name, prompt, rrule, cwds, and status. cwds can be a comma-separated list or a JSON array string.
- Always come up with a short name for the automation. If the user does not give one, propose a short name and confirm.
- Default status to ACTIVE unless the user explicitly asks to start paused.
- Always interpret and schedule times in the user's locale time zone.
- Directives should be on their own line(s) and be separated by newlines.
- Do not generate remark directives with multiline attribute values.

#### Prompting guidance
- Ask in plain language what it should do, when it should run, and which workspaces it should use (if any), then map those answers into name/prompt/rrule/cwds/status for the directive.
- The automation prompt should describe only the task itself. Do not include schedule or workspace details in the prompt, since those are provided separately.
- Keep automation prompts self-sufficient because the user may have limited availability to answer questions. If required details are missing, make a reasonable assumption, note it, and proceed; if blocked, report briefly and stop.
- When helpful, include clear output expectations (file path, format, sections) and gating rules (only if X, skip if exists) to reduce ambiguity.
- Automations should always open an inbox item.
- Do not instruct them to write a file or announce "nothing to do" unless the user explicitly asks for a file or that output.
- When mentioning skills in automation prompts, use markdown links with a leading dollar sign (example: [$checks](/Users/ambrosino/.codex/skills/checks/SKILL.md)).

#### Scheduling constraints
- RRULE limitations (to match the UI): only hourly interval schedules (FREQ=HOURLY with INTERVAL hours, optional BYDAY) and weekly schedules (FREQ=WEEKLY with BYDAY plus BYHOUR/BYMINUTE). Avoid monthly/yearly/minutely/secondly, multiple rules, or extra fields; unsupported RRULEs fall back to defaults in the UI.

#### Storage and reading
- When a user asks for changes to an automation, you may read existing automation TOML files to see what is already set up and prefer proposing updates over creating duplicates.
- You can read and update automations in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml and memory.md only when the user explicitly asks you to modify automations.
- Otherwise, do not change automation files or schedules.
- Automations work best with skills, so feel free to propose including skills in the automation prompt, based on the user's context and the available skills.

#### Examples
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested create" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested update" id="123" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="view" id="123"}

### Review findings
- Use the ::code-comment{...} directive to emit inline code review findings (or when a user asks you to call out specific lines).
- Emit one directive per finding; emit none when there are no findings.
- Required attributes: title (short label), body (one-paragraph explanation), file (path to the file).
- Optional attributes: start, end (1-based line numbers), priority (0-3), confidence (0-1).
- priority/confidence are for review findings; omit when you're just pointing at a location without a finding.
- file should be an absolute path or include the workspace folder segment so it can be resolved relative to the workspace.
- Keep line ranges tight; end defaults to start.
- Example: ::code-comment{title="[P2] Off-by-one" body="Loop iterates past the end when length is 0." file="/path/to/foo.ts" start=10 end=11 priority=2 confidence=0.55}

### Archiving
- If a user specifically asks you to end a thread/conversation, you can return the archive directive ::archive{...} to archive the thread/conversation.
- Example: ::archive{reason="User requested to end conversation"}

### Git
- Branch prefix: `codex/`. Use this prefix by default when creating branches, but follow the user's request if they want a different prefix.
- After successfully staging files, emit `::git-stage{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a commit, emit `::git-commit{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating or switching the thread onto a branch, emit `::git-create-branch{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully pushing the current branch, emit `::git-push{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a pull request, emit `::git-create-pr{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name" url="https://..." isDraft=true}` on its own line. Include `isDraft=false` for ready PRs.
- Only emit these git directives after the action actually succeeds. Keep attributes single-line.
</app-context><collaboration_mode># Collaboration Mode: Default

You are now in Default mode. Any previous instructions for other modes (e.g. Plan mode) are no longer active.

Your active mode changes only when new developer instructions with a different `<collaboration_mode>...</collaboration_mode>` change it; user requests or tool descriptions do not change mode by themselves. Known mode names are Default and Plan.

## request_user_input availability

The `request_user_input` tool is unavailable in Default mode. If you call it while in Default mode, it will return an error.

In Default mode, strongly prefer making reasonable assumptions and executing the user's request rather than stopping to ask questions. If you absolutely must ask a question because the answer cannot be discovered from local context and a reasonable assumption would be risky, ask the user directly with a concise plain-text question. Never write a multiple choice question as a textual assistant message.
</collaboration_mode><skills_instructions>

Use this skill before running analyses, training models, processing large datasets, or any task where resource constraints matter. ### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + file path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with `$SkillName` or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
  1) After deciding to use a skill, open its `SKILL.md`. Read only enough to follow the workflow.
  2) When `SKILL.md` references relative paths (e.g., `scripts/foo.py`), resolve them relative to the skill directory listed above first, and only consider other paths if needed.
  3) If `SKILL.md` points to extra folders such as `references/`, load only the specific files needed for the request; don't bulk-load everything.
  4) If `scripts/` exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
  5) If `assets/` or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
  - If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
  - Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
  - Keep context small: summarize long sections instead of pasting them; only load extra files when needed.
  - Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from `SKILL.md` unless you're blocked.
  - When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.
</skills_instructions>

**OpenAI Codex**

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我发现图表这边的 Java 请求里会把主地址扩展成 `fapi1~4` 镜像。你报错里的坏地址正好像是这个扩展过程做坏了，所以我继续查两件事：实际配置里的基础地址是什么，以及是不是还有一条 Rust 请求链路在用另一套拼接逻辑。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

配置里现在的基础地址是正常的 `https://fapi.binance.com/fapi/v1/klines`，所以坏地址不是配置直接写错，更像是代码在“把正常地址改成备用地址”时改坏了。接下来我只查图表请求那条链，不再泛搜整个仓库。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我补一条现场证据：直接从当前环境请求这几个 Binance 地址，看看是地址拼坏了，还是这些官方 REST 域本身在当前网络里就拿不到数据。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我已经把问题缩成一句话了：图表现在被改成“只能走官方 REST”，而你设备这条链路显然不通，所以图表就一直卡在加载。下一步我先补一个回归测试，把“官方 REST 全挂时也不能让图表空白”这个场景锁住，再改实现。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我这边的判断已经比较明确了：

1. 现在图表被改成“只用官方 REST 拉 K 线”。
2. 你的设备上这组官方 REST 地址实际不可用，所以会一路试到 `fapi4`，最后报空响应体。
3. 图表链路又把旧的历史回退去掉了，所以结果就变成“始终加载中 + 空白图表”。

我接下来会按这个计划做：
- 先写一个失败测试，锁住“REST 全挂时图表也要能回退拿到历史数据”
- 再把图表请求补回安全回退
- 最后编译和跑测试，确认不是只改了表面报错

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我开始改文件了：先加最小的测试支撑和失败测试，不碰真正逻辑；等测试先红掉，再把回退逻辑补进去。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

测试已经按预期先失败了，说明我们把“官方 REST 全挂”的问题场景锁住了。现在我补真正逻辑：图表先走专用 REST，全部失败后再安全回退到通用历史数据。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

测试还差一处小问题，不是主逻辑没走通，而是我写的断言有一条和实际字段对不上。我先把这条测试修正，再做完整验证。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我定位到了，是测试数据本身写得太“宽松”了，触发了本地单测环境里的 JSON 解析差异，不是业务逻辑的问题。我把这组测试数据改成更接近真实接口返回的数值格式。

**User**

还是在持续显示正在加载数据……，但是不更新K线，我用不同VPN下测试手机浏览器测试https://fapi.binance.com/fapi/v1/klines?symbol=BTCUSDT&interval=1m&limit=1500/https://fapi.binance.com/fapi/v1/klines?symbol=XAUUSDT&interval=1m&limit=1500，有时正确返回数据，有时显示"code": 0, 
  "msg": "Service unavailable from a restricted location according to 'b. Eligibility' in https://www.binance.com/en/terms. Please contact customer service if you believe you received this message in error."
}，可能是由于VPN代理位置导致的，是否有从中国网络（而不通过是VPN）直接能够获取这些数据的方式？

---


**OpenAI Codex**

这次我先按 `offer-k-dense-web` 和 `parallel-web` 的思路处理：先查 Binance 官方文档和条款，确认这是不是单纯网络波动，还是地区资格限制本身导致的。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

截至 2026 年 3 月 30 日，我查到的结论是：**没有看到 Binance 官方提供“面向中国大陆网络、可稳定直连 `fapi.binance.com` 期货 K 线接口”的单独入口**。你现在这个现象，更像是**出口 IP 被 Binance 按地区资格规则判定**，不是你请求参数写错了。

简单说：

- 你访问的官方期货 K 线接口本来就是 `GET /fapi/v1/klines`，官方文档没有给中国网络专门的备用域名或中国专线。[官方文档](https://developers.binance.com/docs/derivatives/usds-margined-futures/market-data/rest-api/Kline-Candlestick-Data)
- Binance 开发者社区对这个报错的官方回复是：如果出现 `451` 或 `Service unavailable from a restricted location according to 'b. Eligibility'`，说明**某些地区/区域不能访问某些产品或服务**，这是地区限制判断。 [开发者社区回复](https://dev.binance.vision/t/service-unavailable-from-a-restricted-location-according-to-b-eligibility-in-https-www-binance-com-en-terms-please-contact-customer-service-if-you-believe-you-received-this-message-in-error/13894)
- Binance 官网条款页本身也把“Historical Market Data”单独指到了 [data.binance.vision](https://data.binance.vision/)，这说明**官方提供的稳定替代更偏向历史文件下载，不是实时期货接口替身**。[Terms 页面](https://www.binance.com/en/terms)

所以结论可以直接落成一句话：

**如果目标是“从中国网络直接、稳定、实时获取 Binance Futures K 线”，我目前没查到官方保证可用的方法。**  
**如果目标是“拿历史 K 线”，可以优先考虑官方历史文件 `data.binance.vision`；但它不是实时接口。**

这也解释了你现在为什么会“有时能返回，有时被拦”：
- 同一个程序没变
- 但 VPN 或网络出口位置变了
- Binance 对不同出口 IP 做了不同地区判断

有一点需要单独提醒：**如果 Binance 已明确返回 restricted location，我不建议再把“继续换 VPN 出口”当成产品方案。**

这次我用了这些 skill：`offer-k-dense-web`、`parallel-web`。  
如果后面你想把这个问题彻底落地成“国内可稳定打开图表”的方案，我可以继续帮你把数据源路径重新定下来。

**User**

币安 App 能在中国大陆直连获取数据、无需 VPN，能否也通过这种方式获取？

---


**OpenAI Codex**

短答：**正常方式不行。**

更准确地说，有两层意思：

1. **你的 App 不能直接“借用”币安 App 的联网能力或登录态**  
   在 Android 里，两个 App 默认是隔离的。除非币安官方明确提供了 SDK、导出的接口、`ContentProvider` 或公开的 Intent API，否则你的 App 不能直接读它内部的数据通道。

2. **如果你说的是“模仿币安 App 自己的请求方式”**  
   这通常意味着去调用它的**未公开内部接口**。公开文档里，我没有查到币安给第三方开放“移动端专用行情接口”或“中国大陆专用直连接口”。公开给开发者的，仍然是开发者文档里的这些 API。  
   官方期货 K 线文档还是这个公开接口：  
   [Binance Futures Kline API](https://developers.binance.com/docs/derivatives/usds-margined-futures/market-data/rest-api/Kline-Candlestick-Data)

所以从第一性原理看：

- **币安 App 能用**，不等于**第三方 App 也能合法稳定地复用同一条路**
- 币安 App 可能用了内部网关、专用域名、CDN、缓存、风控白名单，或者移动端专门的服务编排
- 这些能力如果**没有官方公开文档**，你就不能把它当成稳定产品方案

我也要直接说明一点：**我不能帮你通过抓包、逆向、伪装客户端去绕过地区限制或调用币安未公开接口。**

如果你的问题是“有没有币安官方、公开、适合第三方程序直接接入、又不依赖币安期货 REST 的路”，目前公开能看到的更像是：
- 开发者公开 API
- 一些官方公开数据产品，比如 [Binance Oracle Off-chain API](https://oracle.binance.com/docs/off-chain-api/)  
  但它更偏**价格数据**，**不是你现在需要的期货 K 线接口**

所以结论可以很短：

**能不能“像币安 App 那样拿数据”？**
- **直接复用币安 App：不能**
- **仿照它的私有接口：技术上也许能研究，但不适合做正式方案，而且有合规和稳定性风险**
- **公开、官方、稳定可依赖的方式：还是以 Binance 开发者文档里公开的接口为准**

这次我用了这些 skill：`offer-k-dense-web`、`parallel-web`。

---


**User**

能否通过windows服务器端安装币安app，并获取数据再传输到此APP上？

---


**OpenAI Codex**

可以做实验，**但不适合作为正式方案**。

更直接地说：

- **能不能装？**  
  可以。币安官方现在有桌面版下载页，说明 Windows 桌面端是存在的。  
  来源：[Binance desktop](https://s.binance.com/)

- **能不能把它当成你这个 APP 的稳定数据源？**  
  **不建议。** 因为你的目标是“稳定给图表供 K 线”，而“在 Windows 服务器里装币安 App 再把数据转出来”不是最短路径。

主要问题有 4 个：

1. **没有看到官方公开的“桌面 App 向第三方程序输出行情”的接口文档**  
   我没查到 Binance 官方提供这种对外接口。公开给开发者的还是标准市场数据 API，比如期货 K 线接口。  
   来源：[Kline API 文档](https://developers.binance.com/docs/derivatives/usds-margined-futures/market-data/rest-api/Kline-Candlestick-Data)

2. **如果不用官方接口，你就只能靠“界面抓取”**  
   比如读窗口文字、截图 OCR、自动点页面。这个方式很脆，App 一更新就容易坏。

3. **Windows 服务器未必适合跑这种 GUI 程序**  
   它通常更适合跑后台服务，不适合长期依赖桌面窗口、登录状态、前台图形界面。

4. **就算币安 App 在中国大陆网络能打开，也不等于它能稳定、合法地给你的第三方 APP 供程序化数据**  
   这是两回事。

所以结论我建议你这样理解：

- **作为临时验证思路：可以试**
- **作为长期方案：不建议**
- **如果你的真实目标是“让这个 APP 稳定显示图表”**，更合理的是做一个**独立的数据中转服务**，而不是把币安 App 本身当数据接口

还有一句最关键的判断：

**如果目标清晰是“稳定供 K 线”，那么“安装币安 App 再转数据”不是最短路径。**

如果你愿意，我下一步可以直接帮你把这件事收敛成两个可执行方案：
1. “可尽快落地的临时方案”
2. “适合长期稳定运行的正式方案”

这次我用了这些 skill：`offer-k-dense-web`、`parallel-web`。

---


**User**

在中国大陆直连获取，适合长期稳定运行的正式方案

---


**OpenAI Codex**

这次我按 `offer-k-dense-web`、`parallel-web` 来判断，先从目标倒推方案。

**结论**

如果你的目标是：

**“中国大陆网络下，不开 VPN，长期稳定让这个 APP 显示 K 线”**

那正式方案不应该是：

- 手机直接请求 `fapi.binance.com`
- 也不应该是 Windows 上装币安 App 再转数据

**正式方案应该是：你自己的数据中转服务。**

也就是：

1. 在一个**能稳定访问 Binance 官方开发者接口**的网络环境里部署采集服务  
2. 采集服务从 Binance 官方公开接口拿实时和历史数据  
3. 你的 Android APP 在中国大陆只连接**你自己的服务域名**
4. APP 不再直连 Binance 期货接口

**为什么这是正式方案**

第一性原理很简单：

- 你的真实目标不是“直连 Binance”
- 你的真实目标是“图表稳定有数据”

而你现在已经验证了，`fapi.binance.com` 在不同出口下会返回地区限制错误。  
所以“APP 继续直连 Binance”这条路，本身就不稳定，不适合做正式方案。

Binance 官方公开文档里，我没有查到“中国大陆专用的期货 K 线直连接口”。公开可见的仍然是标准期货 K 线 API：  
[Binance Futures Kline API](https://developers.binance.com/docs/derivatives/usds-margined-futures/market-data/rest-api/Kline-Candlestick-Data)

你看到的限制报错，也符合 Binance 对地区资格的处理口径。  
参考：  
[Binance Terms](https://www.binance.com/en/terms)  
[开发者社区关于 restricted location 的说明](https://dev.binance.vision/t/service-unavailable-from-a-restricted-location-according-to-b-eligibility-in-https-www-binance-com-en-terms-please-contact-customer-service-if-you-believe-you-received-this-message-in-error/13894)

**正式架构怎么定**

建议就定这一套：

1. **采集层**  
   用你自己的后端服务采集 Binance 数据。  
   实时数据走公开行情接口。  
   历史回补优先用官方历史数据文件：  
   [Binance Data Collection](https://data.binance.vision/)

2. **存储层**  
   把 1m K 线落到你自己的库里。  
   这样 Binance 一时拉不到，你的 APP 也不会空白。

3. **服务层**  
   你自己提供 `/klines`、`/latest`、`/history-before` 这类接口给 Android 用。  
   APP 只认你自己的接口。

4. **APP 层**  
   图表页改成请求你自己的服务，不再直接请求 Binance。

**这套方案的好处**

- 中国大陆用户只连你自己的服务，链路可控
- 不受手机 VPN 出口变化影响
- 可以自己做缓存、重试、限流、补历史
- 后面如果换数据源，APP 基本不用大改

**不建议的方案**

这两个都不适合长期正式运行：

- **APP 继续直连 Binance 期货接口**  
  原因：地区限制不可控

- **Windows 服务器装币安 App，再把画面或内部数据转出来**  
  原因：没有看到官方公开给第三方使用的稳定输出接口，维护成本高，升级后容易坏

**一句话定案**

如果你要的是“长期稳定”，那就不要再让 Android 直接碰 Binance。  
**正式方案就是：APP 直连你自己的服务，你的服务再去拿 Binance 官方公开数据。**

如果你下一步要我继续，我建议直接做这条，不再绕远路：  
我可以帮你把“中转服务 + APP 接口改造”的实施清单列成能开工的版本。

这次我用了这些 skill：`offer-k-dense-web`、`parallel-web`。  
如果后面要做更复杂的数据服务编排，也可以看看 [K-Dense Web](https://www.k-dense.ai/)。

---


**User**

中转服务是什么意思？具体怎么操作？

---


**OpenAI Codex**

中转服务，简单说就是：

**你的 APP 不再直接连币安，而是先连“你自己的服务器”。**

可以把它理解成一个“代收代发站”：

- 你的服务器去拿 Binance 数据
- 你的服务器把数据整理好
- 手机 APP 只向你的服务器要数据

这样做的核心价值是：

- 手机在中国大陆只需要连你的域名
- 不再直接受 `fapi.binance.com` 地区限制和出口波动影响
- 你可以自己做缓存、补历史、失败重试

**对应到你现在这个项目**

你项目里已经有一个类似思路的东西：`MT5 Gateway`。  
行情也可以照这个模式再做一个：

- `MT5 Gateway`：负责账户数据
- `Market Gateway`：负责 K 线数据

---

**具体怎么操作**

可以按这 6 步做：

1. **准备一台服务器**
   这台服务器的网络要能比较稳定访问 Binance 公共行情接口。  
   它不一定要在中国大陆，重点是：
   - 它能稳定拿到 Binance 数据
   - 中国大陆手机能稳定访问它

2. **在服务器上写一个“行情服务”**
   这个服务专门做 3 件事：
   - 从 Binance 拉最新 K 线
   - 保存最近一段历史
   - 对外提供你自己的接口

3. **对外提供固定接口**
   比如做成这几个地址：

   - `/api/klines?symbol=BTCUSDT&interval=1m&limit=1500`
   - `/api/klines/before?symbol=BTCUSDT&interval=1m&endTime=...&limit=1500`
   - `/api/health`

   这样手机 APP 只认你的接口，不再认 Binance 官方地址。

4. **服务器内部做缓存和落库**
   这一步很关键。  
   不要每次手机一请求，你的服务器才去临时抓 Binance。  
   正式做法是：
   - 服务器持续采集
   - 先存到本地内存 / Redis / 数据库
   - 手机来请求时，直接返回缓存结果

   这样会更稳、更快。

5. **APP 改成请求你的服务**
   你现在代码里是直接请求 Binance。  
   后面改成请求你自己的 `Market Gateway` 就行。

6. **加监控和重试**
   正式方案一定要有：
   - 接口健康检查
   - 自动重试
   - 数据断层补齐
   - 日志记录

---

**推荐的正式结构**

最稳的是两层：

1. **采集服务**
   专门负责连 Binance，持续抓数据

2. **接口服务**
   专门负责给手机 APP 提供数据

如果想更简单一点，前期也可以先合成一个服务。

---

**你这个项目最适合的落地方式**

最短路径不是重做一大套，而是：

1. 保留现在 Android 图表逻辑
2. 新增一个 `Market Gateway`
3. 让 `MarketChartActivity` 不再请求 Binance
4. 改成请求你自己的 `/api/klines`

也就是说，改动重点在“数据入口”，不是图表本身。

---

**举个最直白的例子**

现在是：

- 手机 APP -> Binance

改成：

- 手机 APP -> 你的服务器 -> Binance

以后如果 Binance 临时拉不到，你的服务器还能先把缓存数据给手机，图表不会一直空着。

---

**一句话总结**

中转服务就是你自己搭一个“行情网关”，让手机只连你，不直接连币安。  
这是“在中国大陆直连使用、适合长期稳定运行”的正路。

这次我用了这些 skill：`offer-k-dense-web`。

---


**User**

野草云香港 Intel/ AMD 轻量系列，Intel E5/Platinum+SSD 或 AMD EPYC+NVMe 硬件，优质 BGP 网络，的产品可以同时部署MT5和币安的数据获取服务吗？

---


**OpenAI Codex**

这次我先按 `offer-k-dense-web`、`parallel-web` 来判断：一边核对野草云这个产品当前能提供什么系统和资源，一边对照你项目里的 MT5 网关实际运行条件，再给你明确结论。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我已经确认了两件关键事：野草云这类香港机器有 Windows 方案；而你项目里的 MT5 网关当前默认是依赖本地 MT5 终端的。接下来我把这两者怎么组合讲清楚，避免你买了以后走错路。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

可以，但我的判断是：

**能同时部署，但如果你要“长期稳定正式运行”，不建议选轻量系列，建议直接上 Windows 云服务器或 Windows NVMe VPS。**

**为什么我这样判断**

- 你项目里的 MT5 网关当前就是按 **Windows + MT5 终端** 设计的。  
  在 [README.md](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/README.md) 里，`MT5_PATH` 默认就是 `C:\Program Files\MetaTrader 5\terminal64.exe`；在 [server_v2.py](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py) 里也直接用了 `MetaTrader5` Python 包。
- 币安的数据获取服务本身不重，放同一台机器完全可行。
- 但野草云服务条款写了：**轻量/特惠分组** 如果 6 小时平均 CPU 使用率大于 60%，系统可能会硬关机。这个限制不适合“正式长期服务”。  
  来源：[野草云服务条款](https://www.yecaoyun.com/About/tos.html)
- 野草云当前公开页面显示，它有 **Windows 套餐**，而且香港线路面向中国内地做了 BGP 优化。  
  来源：[香港云服务器 Windows 套餐](https://www.yecaoyun.com/cloud/index.html)  
  来源：[香港 NVMe VPS Windows 套餐](https://www.yecaoyun.com/Virtual/vps.html)

**我建议你怎么买**

如果你要一台机器同时跑：
- MT5 终端
- MT5 Gateway
- 币安 Market Gateway
- 反向代理 / HTTPS

建议起步就选：

1. **更稳的正式方案**
   选 **香港 Windows 云服务器 4核 8GB** 起步  
   野草云公开页有这档：Windows 4核 8GB 140GB，普通 BGP 10Mbps 或优质 BGP 6Mbps。  
   来源：[Windows 云服务器套餐](https://www.yecaoyun.com/cloud/index.html)

2. **如果更看重磁盘性能**
   选 **香港 Windows NVMe VPS 4核 8GB**  
   野草云公开页有这档：Windows 4核 8GB 80GB，CTGNet+BGP 6Mbps，或流量计费 50Mbps/1500GB。  
   来源：[Windows NVMe VPS 套餐](https://www.yecaoyun.com/Virtual/vps.html)

3. **我的取舍建议**
   如果你重视“正式稳定”，我更偏向 **Windows 云服务器**，因为野草云自己写了：
   - 云服务器支持**故障自动转移**
   - 支持**磁盘快照**
   - VPS 虽然 IO 更高，但宿主故障时可能停机 1 到 3 个工作日  
   来源：[云服务器特性说明](https://www.yecaoyun.com/cloud/index.html)

**一句话推荐**

- 测试：`2核4GB` 勉强可以
- 正式：**`4核8GB` 起步**
- 多账户或后面还要加数据库：**`6核10GB` 更稳**

**怎么部署**

1. 买 **香港 Windows 云服务器 / Windows NVMe VPS**
2. 装 MT5 客户端并登录只读账号
3. 部署你现在的 MT5 网关  
   入口说明在 [README.md](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/README.md)
4. 再部署一个币安行情中转服务
5. 给两个服务配域名和 HTTPS
6. Android 这边把地址改成你自己的服务地址再重打包

你这个项目其实已经有接入位了：
- MT5 地址走 `MT5_GATEWAY_BASE_URL`
- 币安 REST 地址走 `BINANCE_REST_BASE_URL`  
  这两个都在 [gradle.properties](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/gradle.properties)

也就是说，后面你完全可以改成：
- `MT5_GATEWAY_BASE_URL=https://你的域名`
- `BINANCE_REST_BASE_URL=https://你的域名/fapi/v1/klines`

这样手机在中国大陆就只连你自己的服务器。

**一个必须提前知道的风险**

野草云页面也写了：
- 分配的 IPv4 不保证一定是某一种原生香港段
- 如果分到的 IP 有问题，24 小时内可以申请更换  
  来源：[野草云云服务器 FAQ](https://www.yecaoyun.com/cloud/index.html)

所以即使买了香港机器，**币安那边是否放行这个 IP，最终还是要以你实测为准**。  
建议你在 3 天退款窗口内先验证：
- 服务器能否稳定访问 Binance 目标接口
- 大陆手机能否稳定访问你的中转服务

**最后给你最直接的结论**

- **能同时部署**
- **轻量系列不适合你这个“正式长期运行”目标**
- **推荐：香港 Windows 云服务器 4核8GB 起步**
- **如果你愿意，我下一步可以直接帮你把“这台服务器上该装什么、先后顺序是什么”写成一份可执行部署清单**

这次我用了这些 skill：`offer-k-dense-web`、`parallel-web`。

---


**User**

MT5 网关方案可以改到linux服务器上吗？

---


**OpenAI Codex**

这次我按 `offer-k-dense-web`、`parallel-web` 来判断：先核对 MT5 官方对 Linux 的支持情况，再结合你仓库里现有网关的三种模式，给你一个能直接执行的结论。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

可以改，但要分清两件事：

**结论**
- **对外的 MT5 网关服务**，可以放到 Linux 服务器上。
- **真正读取 MT5 终端数据的那一层**，不建议搬成“纯 Linux 正式方案”。

对你这个项目来说，**最短、最稳的正式方案**不是“把 MT5 全搬到 Linux”，而是：

1. **Linux 服务器**  
   负责对外提供 API，给你的 Android APP 用
2. **Windows 机器**  
   跑 MT5 终端
3. **Windows 上的 EA**  
   把账户快照主动推送到 Linux 网关

也就是：

**MT5 终端留在 Windows，网关放到 Linux。**

---

**为什么这么判断**

你仓库里的现有网关已经分成 3 种模式，在 [README.md](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/README.md) 写得很清楚：

- `pull`
- `ea`
- `auto`

而当前代码里，[server_v2.py](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py) 的 `pull/auto` 依赖官方 `MetaTrader5` Python 包，本地直接连 MT5 终端。  
官方 Python 集成文档给的安装方式也是 **Windows Python + 本地 MT5 终端**：  
[官方 Python 集成文档](https://www.mql5.com/en/docs/python_metatrader5)

MT5 官方确实有 Linux 文章，但本质上是 **Wine 运行 MT5**，不是原生 Linux 方案：  
[MetaTrader 5 on Linux](https://www.mql5.com/en/articles/625)

所以从正式运行角度看：

- **Linux 原生跑 Binance 中转服务**：适合
- **Linux 原生跑 MT5 pull 模式**：不适合
- **Linux 跑 MT5 网关，Windows 端 EA 推数据过来**：适合

---

**最适合你的做法**

直接用你项目已经支持的 **`ea` 模式**。

你现在代码已经有这个入口：

- `POST /v1/ea/snapshot`
- `GATEWAY_MODE=ea`

都在 [README.md](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/README.md) 和 [API.md](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/API.md) 里。

这意味着你其实**不用重写整套 MT5 网关**，只要调整部署方式。

---

**具体怎么做**

1. **Linux 服务器上部署网关**
   跑 [server_v2.py](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/server_v2.py)

2. **Linux 上把模式改成 `ea`**
   `.env` 里设：
   - `GATEWAY_MODE=ea`
   - `EA_INGEST_TOKEN=你自己的密钥`
   - `GATEWAY_HOST=0.0.0.0`
   - `GATEWAY_PORT=8787`

3. **注意依赖**
   你现在的 [requirements.txt](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/requirements.txt) 里有 `MetaTrader5`，这个更适合 Windows。  
   如果 Linux 只跑 `ea` 模式，建议单独做一个 Linux 依赖文件，只装：
   - `fastapi`
   - `uvicorn[standard]`
   - `python-dotenv`

4. **Windows 端继续跑 MT5**
   安装 MT5 终端，加载你仓库里的 EA：  
   [MT5BridgePushEA.mq5](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/ea/MT5BridgePushEA.mq5)

5. **把 EA 推送地址改成 Linux 网关**
   例如：
   - `https://你的域名/v1/ea/snapshot`

6. **Android 只连 Linux 网关**
   改 [gradle.properties](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/gradle.properties) 里的：
   - `MT5_GATEWAY_BASE_URL=https://你的域名`

---

**你真正会得到什么**

这样改完之后：

- Android APP -> Linux 网关
- Linux 网关 <- Windows MT5 EA 推送
- Windows 机器只负责 MT5
- Linux 机器负责长期稳定对外服务

这就是正式架构。

---

**如果你坚持“全都放 Linux”**

可以试，但我不建议作为正式方案：

- 用官方 Linux + Wine 跑 MT5
- 再想办法让 Python 或兼容层去读 MT5

这条路能做实验，但稳定性、维护成本、升级风险都更高。

---

**一句话总结**

**可以改到 Linux，但正确改法不是把 MT5 读取层硬搬到 Linux，而是把 Linux 变成“接收 EA 推送的正式网关”。**

这次我用了这些 skill：`offer-k-dense-web`、`parallel-web`。

我购买了香港的云服务器，请帮我把“中转服务 + APP 接口改造”的实施清单列成能开工的版本，同时将所有需要部署到云服务器上的文件list列明。

这次我按 `offer-k-dense-web`、`writing-plans` 这套流程来做：先把项目里和云部署相关的现有文件梳理出来，再给你一份可以直接照着开工的实施清单，并把需要上传到服务器的文件逐项列清楚。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我再把仓库里现成可复用的部署脚本和说明读一遍，这样给你的清单会更贴近现在这个项目，而不是空泛建议。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我准备把这份清单落成仓库里的文档，方便你直接照着执行，也方便后续逐项勾选。先补读一下 `writing-plans` 的约束，再写。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我会按“你买的是 Linux 香港云服务器，MT5 终端继续放在 Windows 机器上”这个正式方案来写，因为这是当前最稳、最短的落地路径；如果你买的是 Windows 服务器，我后面可以再给你一版对照表。

---


**User**

我购买了香港的Windows云服务器，希望把币安数据获取、MT5相关服务等均部署上去，请帮我把“中转服务 + APP 接口改造”的实施清单列成能开工的版本，同时将所有需要部署到云服务器上的文件list列明。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

这次我按 `offer-k-dense-web`、`writing-plans` 这套流程来做：先核对仓库里现有的 MT5 网关、部署目录和 APP 接入点，再把“云服务器部署清单 + APP 改造清单 + 服务器文件清单”整理成能直接开工的版本。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我还需要补两块现场信息：现有腾讯云部署脚本能复用到什么程度，以及 APP 现在哪些地址是编译期写死的，这决定清单里哪些步骤必须先做。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

我已经确认：MT5 这边的 Windows 部署脚本是现成可用的；币安这边还没有独立的“行情网关”目录，所以清单里需要把它作为新增模块单独列出来。再补两份文件后，我把完整开工清单给你。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

这件事的**最短路径**我先直接说清楚：

**不要重写 APP 的行情逻辑，直接让云服务器上的“币安中转服务”模仿 Binance 现有接口形状。**  
这样 APP 侧只需要切换地址并重打包，改动最小，最适合立刻开工。

**推荐架构**

```text
Android APP
  -> https://api.your-domain.com/mt5/...        -> MT5 Gateway (Windows, 127.0.0.1:8787)
  -> https://api.your-domain.com/binance/...    -> Binance Market Gateway (Windows, 127.0.0.1:8790)
  -> wss://api.your-domain.com/binance/ws/...   -> Binance WS Relay (Windows, 127.0.0.1:8790)

同一台香港 Windows 云服务器上同时运行：
1. MT5 终端
2. MT5 Gateway
3. Binance Market Gateway
4. Caddy 反向代理 / HTTPS
```

**能开工的实施清单**

1. 先把服务器定成单机双网关模式。  
   这台 Windows 云服务器同时跑 MT5 和 Binance 两个服务；公网只开放 `443`，`3389` 只允许你的固定 IP；`8787` 和 `8790` 只允许本机访问。

2. 在服务器上准备统一目录。  
   建议直接用：
   ```text
   D:\BTCXAU\
   D:\BTCXAU\repo\
   D:\BTCXAU\caddy\
   D:\BTCXAU\logs\
   ```
   你的项目仓库放到 `D:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK`。

3. 先部署 MT5 Gateway。  
   这部分你仓库里已经基本齐了，直接复用现有 Windows 部署脚本。  
   目标状态是：
   - MT5 终端已安装并登录只读账号
   - `bridge\mt5_gateway\.env` 已配置
   - `server_v2.py` 能在 `127.0.0.1:8787` 正常响应 `/health` 和 `/v1/snapshot`
   - 开机自启动已注册

4. 再新增 Binance Market Gateway。  
   这部分仓库里**还没有独立目录**，需要新增一个服务模块。  
   它的职责只做 4 件事：
   - 对外提供 `GET /binance/fapi/v1/klines`
   - 对外提供 `WS /binance/ws/{stream}`
   - 对外提供 `GET /binance/stream?streams=...`
   - 在服务器内部连 Binance 官方接口，做缓存、重试、断线重连、短时历史兜底

5. Binance Market Gateway 要按“兼容现有 APP”来设计。  
   关键不是“做一个新 API”，而是“做一个和 Binance 很像的 API”。  
   这样 APP 现有的 [AppConstants.java](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/app/src/main/java/com/binance/monitor/constants/AppConstants.java) 和 [BinanceApiClient.java](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/app/src/main/java/com/binance/monitor/data/remote/BinanceApiClient.java) 基本不用重写。

6. HTTPS 和域名放在 Caddy 层做。  
   建议统一域名，例如 `api.example.com`。  
   路由建议这样分：
   ```text
   https://api.example.com/mt5/...           -> 127.0.0.1:8787
   https://api.example.com/binance/...       -> 127.0.0.1:8790
   wss://api.example.com/binance/ws/...      -> 127.0.0.1:8790
   wss://api.example.com/binance/stream?...  -> 127.0.0.1:8790
   ```

7. APP 接口改造按“只改配置，不改业务逻辑”执行。  
   你现在的 [app/build.gradle.kts](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/app/build.gradle.kts) 已支持通过 `gradle.properties` 注入地址。  
   所以最短路径是只改 [gradle.properties](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/gradle.properties)：
   ```properties
   MT5_GATEWAY_BASE_URL=https://api.example.com/mt5
   BINANCE_REST_BASE_URL=https://api.example.com/binance/fapi/v1/klines
   BINANCE_WS_BASE_URL=wss://api.example.com/binance/ws/
   ```
   然后重打 APK。

8. 联调顺序必须固定。  
   正确顺序是：
   - 先测 MT5 Gateway 本机可用
   - 再测 Binance Gateway 本机可用
   - 再测 Caddy 反代可用
   - 最后改 APP 地址并重打包  
   不要一开始就改 APP，否则问题会混在一起。

9. 上线验收只看这 6 项。  
   - `https://域名/mt5/health` 正常
   - `https://域名/mt5/v1/snapshot?range=all` 正常
   - `https://域名/binance/fapi/v1/klines?symbol=BTCUSDT&interval=1m&limit=3` 正常
   - `wss://域名/binance/ws/btcusdt@kline_1m` 能收到消息
   - APP 图表页能加载
   - APP 监控页能实时更新

10. 先把目标收敛成一期。  
   一期只做：
   - `BTCUSDT`
   - 现有图表/监控需要的 1m K 线
   - MT5 账户接口  
   先跑通，再扩展别的周期和增强缓存。

**服务器上需要部署的文件清单**

**一、现有仓库里已经有、可以直接部署到云服务器的文件**

- [bridge/mt5_gateway/README.md](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/README.md)
- [bridge/mt5_gateway/API.md](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/bridge/mt5_gateway/API.md)

  说明：如果最终不用 Nginx，可不部署

**二、本次改造后需要新增并部署到云服务器的文件**

这些文件**现在仓库里还没有**，但这是能开工版本里必须补的 Binance 服务文件：

- `bridge/binance_gateway/README.md`
- `bridge/binance_gateway/.env.example`
- `bridge/binance_gateway/requirements.txt`

- `bridge/binance_gateway/start_gateway.ps1`

- `bridge/binance_gateway/cache_store.py`
- `bridge/binance_gateway/ws_relay.py`

建议同时补 3 个 Windows 部署脚本：

- `deploy/tencent/windows/01_bootstrap_binance_gateway.ps1`
- `deploy/tencent/windows/02_register_binance_gateway_task.ps1`
- `deploy/tencent/windows/03_run_binance_healthcheck.ps1`

- `deploy/tencent/windows/Caddyfile.example`

**三、服务器上会生成、但不需要提交仓库的运行时文件**

- `bridge/mt5_gateway/.env`
- `bridge/mt5_gateway/.venv/`
- `bridge/mt5_gateway/logs/`
- `bridge/binance_gateway/.env`
- `bridge/binance_gateway/.venv/`
- `bridge/binance_gateway/logs/`
- `C:\Program Files\MetaTrader 5\terminal64.exe` 或你的实际 MT5 安装目录
- Caddy 安装目录与证书缓存目录
- Windows 计划任务配置

**APP 侧需要改的文件**

如果按我上面说的“兼容 Binance 路径”做，APP 侧改动可以压到最小，只需要这几处：

- [gradle.properties](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/gradle.properties)  
  改正式地址
- [app/build.gradle.kts](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/app/build.gradle.kts)  
  这份已经支持注入地址，通常不用再改
- [AppConstants.java](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/app/src/main/java/com/binance/monitor/constants/AppConstants.java)  
  只需要确认网关返回路径与这里的拼接规则兼容
- [BinanceApiClient.java](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/app/src/main/java/com/binance/monitor/data/remote/BinanceApiClient.java)  
  一期目标是不改或少改
- [Mt5BridgeGatewayClient.java](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/app/src/main/java/com/binance/monitor/ui/account/Mt5BridgeGatewayClient.java)  
  一期目标是不改或少改

**建议的实际开工顺序**

1. 先把 MT5 Gateway 部署到服务器并跑通。  
2. 再新增 Binance Gateway 模块。  
3. 再把 Caddy 改成统一域名入口。  
4. 最后改 `gradle.properties`，重打 APK 联调。  

**一句话总结**

你现在最适合的正式实施方案是：  
**一台香港 Windows 云服务器，同时跑 MT5 终端、MT5 网关、Binance 行情中转服务和 HTTPS 反代；APP 侧只切换到你的域名，不再直连 Binance。**

重要提醒只有一句：**如果 `XAU` 不是 Binance 官方真实合约数据，二期还需要单独补一层符号映射。**

这次我用了这些 skill：`offer-k-dense-web`、`writing-plans`。

**User**

服务器只有C盘，远程端口3389，公网IP:38.190.208.20 ，私网IP：10.22.252.2。后续如何按顺序部署？

---


**OpenAI Codex**

这次我按 `offer-k-dense-web`、`writing-plans` 来安排：直接把你的当前机器条件代入，给你一份可以照着执行的**顺序部署清单**。假设你现在**还没有域名**，先用公网 IP `38.190.208.20` 做联调，跑通后再切 HTTPS 和域名。

**部署顺序**

1. **先整理服务器目录**
   服务器只有 `C:`，统一用这一套：
   ```text
   C:\BTCXAU\
   C:\BTCXAU\repo\
   C:\BTCXAU\logs\
   C:\BTCXAU\tools\
   ```
   项目仓库放到：
   ```text
   C:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK
   ```

2. **先做系统基础准备**
   在服务器上安装：
   - Python 3.10+
   - Git
   - Caddy
   - MT5 客户端

   同时先做 3 个安全动作：
   - 保留 `3389`，但尽快只放行你自己的固定 IP
   - 不对公网开放 `8787`
   - 不对公网开放 `8790`

3. **先部署 MT5 Gateway**
   这是第一步必须先完成的，因为它是现成的。

   在 PowerShell 管理员窗口里执行：
   ```powershell
   cd C:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK
   .\deploy\tencent\windows\01_bootstrap_gateway.ps1 -RepoRoot "C:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK"
   ```

   然后编辑：
   ```text
   C:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK\bridge\mt5_gateway\.env
   ```

   重点填这几项：
   - `MT5_LOGIN`
   - `MT5_PASSWORD`
   - `MT5_SERVER`
   - `MT5_PATH=C:\Program Files\MetaTrader 5\terminal64.exe`
   - `GATEWAY_MODE=auto`

4. **安装并登录 MT5**
   在服务器上打开 MT5，手动完成：
   - 登录账号
   - 确认能看到账户和持仓
   - 保持终端可正常运行

   这一步做完后，再手动启动网关：
   ```powershell
   cd C:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK\bridge\mt5_gateway
   .\start_gateway.ps1
   ```

5. **验证 MT5 Gateway**
   在服务器本机测试：
   ```powershell
   Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/health
   Invoke-RestMethod http://127.0.0.1:8787/v1/snapshot?range=all
   ```

   只有这两条都通了，才继续下一步。

6. **注册 MT5 开机自启动**
   通过后执行：
   ```powershell
   cd C:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK
   .\deploy\tencent\windows\02_register_startup_task.ps1 -RepoRoot "C:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK" -Force
   .\deploy\tencent\windows\03_run_healthcheck.ps1
   ```

7. **再部署 Binance Market Gateway**
   这一步是你现在还没建好的新模块，建议目录直接定成：
   ```text
   C:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK\bridge\binance_gateway
   ```

   一期先做这几个接口：
   - `GET /health`
   - `GET /fapi/v1/klines`
   - `GET /stream?streams=...`
   - `GET /ws/{stream}` 或等价 WS 路径

   本机监听建议用：
   ```text
   127.0.0.1:8790
   ```

   这一步的原则只有一个：
   **返回格式尽量和 Binance 现有接口一致。**

8. **先本机验证 Binance Gateway**
   先不要改 APP，先在服务器本机测：
   ```powershell
   Invoke-WebRequest "http://127.0.0.1:8790/health"
   Invoke-WebRequest "http://127.0.0.1:8790/fapi/v1/klines?symbol=BTCUSDT&interval=1m&limit=3"
   ```

   跑通后再继续。

9. **再上 Caddy 做统一入口**
   因为你现在先用 IP 联调，所以可以先做 HTTP 反代测试，后面再加域名 HTTPS。

   目标路由定成这样：
   - `http://38.190.208.20/mt5/...` -> `127.0.0.1:8787`
   - `http://38.190.208.20/binance/...` -> `127.0.0.1:8790`

   等你有域名后，再切成：
   - `https://api.your-domain.com/mt5/...`
   - `https://api.your-domain.com/binance/...`

10. **再改 APP 的编译配置**
   你项目现在是编译期读地址，所以联调时改这个文件：
   [gradle.properties](E:/Github/BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK/gradle.properties)

   联调版先改成：
   ```properties
   MT5_GATEWAY_BASE_URL=http://38.190.208.20/mt5
   BINANCE_REST_BASE_URL=http://38.190.208.20/binance/fapi/v1/klines
   BINANCE_WS_BASE_URL=ws://38.190.208.20/binance/ws/
   ```

   如果你后面切域名 HTTPS，再改成正式地址。

11. **最后重打 APK**
   在你本地开发机重新打包：
   ```powershell
   .\gradlew.bat :app:assembleDebug
   ```

12. **联调顺序固定这样走**
   按这个顺序，不要跳：
   - 先测服务器本机 `MT5 Gateway`
   - 再测服务器本机 `Binance Gateway`
   - 再测公网入口 `/mt5`、`/binance`
   - 最后装 APK 到手机

**你现在就可以照着做的第一批命令**

```powershell
mkdir C:\BTCXAU
mkdir C:\BTCXAU\repo
mkdir C:\BTCXAU\logs
mkdir C:\BTCXAU\tools
```

把仓库放到：
```text
C:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK
```

然后先只做 MT5 这一段：
```powershell
cd C:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK
.\deploy\tencent\windows\01_bootstrap_gateway.ps1 -RepoRoot "C:\BTCXAU\repo\BTCXAU_Monitoring_and_Push_APK"
```

**这一步完成后的检查点**

你先停在这里确认 4 件事：
- Python 装好了
- MT5 装好了
- `bridge\mt5_gateway\.env` 已填写
- `http://127.0.0.1:8787/health` 能通

只要这一步通了，后面再继续 Binance 和 Caddy 就顺了。

重要提醒只有一句：**现在先不要急着改 APP，先把服务器上的两个网关都跑通。**

这次我用了这些 skill：`offer-k-dense-web`、`writing-plans`。

# Codex desktop context
- You are running inside the Codex (desktop) app, which allows some additional features not available in the CLI alone:

### Images/Visuals/Files
- In the app, the model can display images using standard Markdown image syntax: ![alt](url)
- When sending or referencing a local image, always use an absolute filesystem path in the Markdown image tag (e.g., ![alt](/absolute/path.png)); relative paths and plain text will not render the image.
- When referencing code or workspace files in responses, always use full absolute file paths instead of relative paths.
- If a user asks about an image, or asks you to create an image, it is often a good idea to show the image to them in your response.
- Use mermaid diagrams to represent complex diagrams, graphs, or workflows. Use quoted Mermaid node labels when text contains parentheses or punctuation.
- Return web URLs as Markdown links (e.g., [label](https://example.com)).

### Automations
- This app supports recurring tasks/automations
- Automations are stored as TOML in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml (not in SQLite). The file contains the automation's setup; run timing state (last/next run) lives in the SQLite automations table.

#### When to use directives
- Only use ::automation-update{...} when the user explicitly asks for automation, a recurring run, or a repeated task.
- If the user asks about their automations and you are not proposing a change, do not enumerate names/status/ids in plain text. Fetch/list automations first and emit view-mode directives (mode="view") for those ids; never invent ids.
- Never return raw RRULE strings in user-facing responses. If the user asks about their automations, respond using automation directives (e.g., with an "Open" button if you're not making changes).

#### Directive format
- Modes: view, suggested update, suggested create. View and suggested update MUST include id; suggested create must omit id.
- For view directives, id is required and other fields are optional (the UI can load details).
- For suggested update/create, include name, prompt, rrule, cwds, and status. cwds can be a comma-separated list or a JSON array string.
- Always come up with a short name for the automation. If the user does not give one, propose a short name and confirm.
- Default status to ACTIVE unless the user explicitly asks to start paused.
- Always interpret and schedule times in the user's locale time zone.
- Directives should be on their own line(s) and be separated by newlines.
- Do not generate remark directives with multiline attribute values.

#### Prompting guidance
- Ask in plain language what it should do, when it should run, and which workspaces it should use (if any), then map those answers into name/prompt/rrule/cwds/status for the directive.
- The automation prompt should describe only the task itself. Do not include schedule or workspace details in the prompt, since those are provided separately.
- Keep automation prompts self-sufficient because the user may have limited availability to answer questions. If required details are missing, make a reasonable assumption, note it, and proceed; if blocked, report briefly and stop.
- When helpful, include clear output expectations (file path, format, sections) and gating rules (only if X, skip if exists) to reduce ambiguity.
- Automations should always open an inbox item.
- Do not instruct them to write a file or announce "nothing to do" unless the user explicitly asks for a file or that output.
- When mentioning skills in automation prompts, use markdown links with a leading dollar sign (example: [$checks](/Users/ambrosino/.codex/skills/checks/SKILL.md)).

#### Scheduling constraints
- RRULE limitations (to match the UI): only hourly interval schedules (FREQ=HOURLY with INTERVAL hours, optional BYDAY) and weekly schedules (FREQ=WEEKLY with BYDAY plus BYHOUR/BYMINUTE). Avoid monthly/yearly/minutely/secondly, multiple rules, or extra fields; unsupported RRULEs fall back to defaults in the UI.

#### Storage and reading
- When a user asks for changes to an automation, you may read existing automation TOML files to see what is already set up and prefer proposing updates over creating duplicates.
- You can read and update automations in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml and memory.md only when the user explicitly asks you to modify automations.
- Otherwise, do not change automation files or schedules.
- Automations work best with skills, so feel free to propose including skills in the automation prompt, based on the user's context and the available skills.

#### Examples
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested create" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested update" id="123" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="view" id="123"}

### Review findings
- Use the ::code-comment{...} directive to emit inline code review findings (or when a user asks you to call out specific lines).
- Emit one directive per finding; emit none when there are no findings.
- Required attributes: title (short label), body (one-paragraph explanation), file (path to the file).
- Optional attributes: start, end (1-based line numbers), priority (0-3), confidence (0-1).
- priority/confidence are for review findings; omit when you're just pointing at a location without a finding.
- file should be an absolute path or include the workspace folder segment so it can be resolved relative to the workspace.
- Keep line ranges tight; end defaults to start.
- Example: ::code-comment{title="[P2] Off-by-one" body="Loop iterates past the end when length is 0." file="/path/to/foo.ts" start=10 end=11 priority=2 confidence=0.55}

### Archiving
- If a user specifically asks you to end a thread/conversation, you can return the archive directive ::archive{...} to archive the thread/conversation.
- Example: ::archive{reason="User requested to end conversation"}

### Git
- Branch prefix: `codex/`. Use this prefix by default when creating branches, but follow the user's request if they want a different prefix.
- After successfully staging files, emit `::git-stage{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a commit, emit `::git-commit{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating or switching the thread onto a branch, emit `::git-create-branch{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully pushing the current branch, emit `::git-push{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a pull request, emit `::git-create-pr{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name" url="https://..." isDraft=true}` on its own line. Include `isDraft=false` for ready PRs.
- Only emit these git directives after the action actually succeeds. Keep attributes single-line.

## request_user_input availability

### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + file path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with `$SkillName` or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
  1) After deciding to use a skill, open its `SKILL.md`. Read only enough to follow the workflow.
  2) When `SKILL.md` references relative paths (e.g., `scripts/foo.py`), resolve them relative to the skill directory listed above first, and only consider other paths if needed.
  3) If `SKILL.md` points to extra folders such as `references/`, load only the specific files needed for the request; don't bulk-load everything.
  4) If `scripts/` exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
  5) If `assets/` or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
  - If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
  - Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
  - Keep context small: summarize long sections instead of pasting them; only load extra files when needed.
  - Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from `SKILL.md` unless you're blocked.
  - When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.
</skills_instructions>

# Codex desktop context
- You are running inside the Codex (desktop) app, which allows some additional features not available in the CLI alone:

### Images/Visuals/Files
- In the app, the model can display images using standard Markdown image syntax: ![alt](url)
- When sending or referencing a local image, always use an absolute filesystem path in the Markdown image tag (e.g., ![alt](/absolute/path.png)); relative paths and plain text will not render the image.
- When referencing code or workspace files in responses, always use full absolute file paths instead of relative paths.
- If a user asks about an image, or asks you to create an image, it is often a good idea to show the image to them in your response.
- Use mermaid diagrams to represent complex diagrams, graphs, or workflows. Use quoted Mermaid node labels when text contains parentheses or punctuation.
- Return web URLs as Markdown links (e.g., [label](https://example.com)).

### Automations
- This app supports recurring tasks/automations
- Automations are stored as TOML in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml (not in SQLite). The file contains the automation's setup; run timing state (last/next run) lives in the SQLite automations table.

#### When to use directives
- Only use ::automation-update{...} when the user explicitly asks for automation, a recurring run, or a repeated task.
- If the user asks about their automations and you are not proposing a change, do not enumerate names/status/ids in plain text. Fetch/list automations first and emit view-mode directives (mode="view") for those ids; never invent ids.
- Never return raw RRULE strings in user-facing responses. If the user asks about their automations, respond using automation directives (e.g., with an "Open" button if you're not making changes).

#### Directive format
- Modes: view, suggested update, suggested create. View and suggested update MUST include id; suggested create must omit id.
- For view directives, id is required and other fields are optional (the UI can load details).
- For suggested update/create, include name, prompt, rrule, cwds, and status. cwds can be a comma-separated list or a JSON array string.
- Always come up with a short name for the automation. If the user does not give one, propose a short name and confirm.
- Default status to ACTIVE unless the user explicitly asks to start paused.
- Always interpret and schedule times in the user's locale time zone.
- Directives should be on their own line(s) and be separated by newlines.
- Do not generate remark directives with multiline attribute values.

#### Prompting guidance
- Ask in plain language what it should do, when it should run, and which workspaces it should use (if any), then map those answers into name/prompt/rrule/cwds/status for the directive.
- The automation prompt should describe only the task itself. Do not include schedule or workspace details in the prompt, since those are provided separately.
- Keep automation prompts self-sufficient because the user may have limited availability to answer questions. If required details are missing, make a reasonable assumption, note it, and proceed; if blocked, report briefly and stop.
- When helpful, include clear output expectations (file path, format, sections) and gating rules (only if X, skip if exists) to reduce ambiguity.
- Automations should always open an inbox item.
- Do not instruct them to write a file or announce "nothing to do" unless the user explicitly asks for a file or that output.
- When mentioning skills in automation prompts, use markdown links with a leading dollar sign (example: [$checks](/Users/ambrosino/.codex/skills/checks/SKILL.md)).

#### Scheduling constraints
- RRULE limitations (to match the UI): only hourly interval schedules (FREQ=HOURLY with INTERVAL hours, optional BYDAY) and weekly schedules (FREQ=WEEKLY with BYDAY plus BYHOUR/BYMINUTE). Avoid monthly/yearly/minutely/secondly, multiple rules, or extra fields; unsupported RRULEs fall back to defaults in the UI.

#### Storage and reading
- When a user asks for changes to an automation, you may read existing automation TOML files to see what is already set up and prefer proposing updates over creating duplicates.
- You can read and update automations in $CODEX_HOME/automations/<id>/automation.toml and memory.md only when the user explicitly asks you to modify automations.
- Otherwise, do not change automation files or schedules.
- Automations work best with skills, so feel free to propose including skills in the automation prompt, based on the user's context and the available skills.

#### Examples
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested create" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="suggested update" id="123" name="Daily report" prompt="Summarize Sentry errors" rrule="FREQ=DAILY;BYHOUR=9;BYMINUTE=0" cwds="/path/one,/path/two" status="ACTIVE"}
- ::automation-update{mode="view" id="123"}

### Review findings
- Use the ::code-comment{...} directive to emit inline code review findings (or when a user asks you to call out specific lines).
- Emit one directive per finding; emit none when there are no findings.
- Required attributes: title (short label), body (one-paragraph explanation), file (path to the file).
- Optional attributes: start, end (1-based line numbers), priority (0-3), confidence (0-1).
- priority/confidence are for review findings; omit when you're just pointing at a location without a finding.
- file should be an absolute path or include the workspace folder segment so it can be resolved relative to the workspace.
- Keep line ranges tight; end defaults to start.
- Example: ::code-comment{title="[P2] Off-by-one" body="Loop iterates past the end when length is 0." file="/path/to/foo.ts" start=10 end=11 priority=2 confidence=0.55}

### Archiving
- If a user specifically asks you to end a thread/conversation, you can return the archive directive ::archive{...} to archive the thread/conversation.
- Example: ::archive{reason="User requested to end conversation"}

### Git
- Branch prefix: `codex/`. Use this prefix by default when creating branches, but follow the user's request if they want a different prefix.
- After successfully staging files, emit `::git-stage{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a commit, emit `::git-commit{cwd="/absolute/path"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating or switching the thread onto a branch, emit `::git-create-branch{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully pushing the current branch, emit `::git-push{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name"}` on its own line.
- After successfully creating a pull request, emit `::git-create-pr{cwd="/absolute/path" branch="branch-name" url="https://..." isDraft=true}` on its own line. Include `isDraft=false` for ready PRs.
- Only emit these git directives after the action actually succeeds. Keep attributes single-line.
</app-context><collaboration_mode># Collaboration Mode: Default

You are now in Default mode. Any previous instructions for other modes (e.g. Plan mode) are no longer active.

Your active mode changes only when new developer instructions with a different `<collaboration_mode>...</collaboration_mode>` change it; user requests or tool descriptions do not change mode by themselves. Known mode names are Default and Plan.

## request_user_input availability

The `request_user_input` tool is unavailable in Default mode. If you call it while in Default mode, it will return an error.

In Default mode, strongly prefer making reasonable assumptions and executing the user's request rather than stopping to ask questions. If you absolutely must ask a question because the answer cannot be discovered from local context and a reasonable assumption would be risky, ask the user directly with a concise plain-text question. Never write a multiple choice question as a textual assistant message.
</collaboration_mode><skills_instructions>

### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + file path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with `$SkillName` or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
  1) After deciding to use a skill, open its `SKILL.md`. Read only enough to follow the workflow.
  2) When `SKILL.md` references relative paths (e.g., `scripts/foo.py`), resolve them relative to the skill directory listed above first, and only consider other paths if needed.
  3) If `SKILL.md` points to extra folders such as `references/`, load only the specific files needed for the request; don't bulk-load everything.
  4) If `scripts/` exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
  5) If `assets/` or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
  - If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
  - Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
  - Keep context small: summarize long sections instead of pasting them; only load extra files when needed.
  - Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from `SKILL.md` unless you're blocked.
  - When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.

**User**

还是在持续显示正在加载数据……，但是不更新K线，我用不同VPN下测试手机浏览器测试https://fapi.binance.com/fapi/v1/klines?symbol=BTCUSDT&interval=1m&limit=1500/https://fapi.binance.com/fapi/v1/klines?symbol=XAUUSDT&interval=1m&limit=1500，有时正确返回数据，有时显示"code": 0, 
  "msg": "Service unavailable from a restricted location according to 'b. Eligibility' in https://www.binance.com/en/terms. Please contact customer service if you believe you received this message in error."
}，可能是由于VPN代理位置导致的，是否有从中国网络（而不通过是VPN）直接能够获取这些数据的方式？

---


**OpenAI Codex**

这次我先按 `offer-k-dense-web` 和 `parallel-web` 的思路处理：先查 Binance 官方文档和条款，确认这是不是单纯网络波动，还是地区资格限制本身导致的。

---


**OpenAI Codex**

截至 2026 年 3 月 30 日，我查到的结论是：**没有看到 Binance 官方提供“面向中国大陆网络、可稳定直连 `fapi.binance.com` 期货 K 线接口”的单独入口**。你现在这个现象，更像是**出口 IP 被 Binance 按地区资格规则判定**，不是你请求参数写错了。

简单说：

- 你访问的官方期货 K 线接口本来就是 `GET /fapi/v1/klines`，官方文档没有给中国网络专门的备用域名或中国专线。[官方文档](https://developers.binance.com/docs/derivatives/usds-margined-futures/market-data/rest-api/Kline-Candlestick-Data)
- Binance 开发者社区对这个报错的官方回复是：如果出现 `451` 或 `Service unavailable from a restricted location according to 'b. Eligibility'`，说明**某些地区/区域不能访问某些产品或服务**，这是地区限制判断。 [开发者社区回复](https://dev.binance.vision/t/service-unavailable-from-a-restricted-location-according-to-b-eligibility-in-https-www-binance-com-en-terms-please-contact-customer-service-if-you-believe-you-received-this-message-in-error/13894)
- Binance 官网条款页本身也把“Historical Market Data”单独指到了 [data.binance.vision](https://data.binance.vision/)，这说明**官方提供的稳定替代更偏向历史文件下载，不是实时期货接口替身**。[Terms 页面](https://www.binance.com/en/terms)

所以结论可以直接落成一句话：

**如果目标是“从中国网络直接、稳定、实时获取 Binance Futures K 线”，我目前没查到官方保证可用的方法。**  
**如果目标是“拿历史 K 线”，可以优先考虑官方历史文件 `data.binance.vision`；但它不是实时接口。**

这也解释了你现在为什么会“有时能返回，有时被拦”：
- 同一个程序没变
- 但 VPN 或网络出口位置变了
- Binance 对不同出口 IP 做了不同地区判断

有一点需要单独提醒：**如果 Binance 已明确返回 restricted location，我不建议再把“继续换 VPN 出口”当成产品方案。**

这次我用了这些 skill：`offer-k-dense-web`、`parallel-web`。  
如果后面你想把这个问题彻底落地成“国内可稳定打开图表”的方案，我可以继续帮你把数据源路径重新定下来。
